What is Mufrad? The Basic Unit of Logic
Defines mufrad and primary division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given term is mufrad or murakkab based on the definition from the passage.

Core Idea
Mufrad is the simple term that cannot be broken into parts each carrying meaning.

Before we can analyse definitions and arguments, we must understand the basic units of language. The logician calls these units 'mufrad' (simple) and 'murakkab' (compound). This lesson defines mufrad and teaches you how to recognize it.

Guided Path
1
Find the definition of mufrad
Look at the opening Arabic: 'المفرد: غير المركب'. This negative definition states that a mufrad is whatever is not a compound.
2
Understand the division of lafz
The author divides uttered expression (lafz) into mufrad and murakkab. There is no third category.
3
Apply the definition to examples
For a word like 'kitab' (book), do its parts (kaf, ta, ba) indicate part of the meaning 'book'? No, so it is mufrad. For 'teacher's pen', the words 'teacher' and 'pen' each contribute meaning, so it is murakkab.
Later parts of the passage confirm: 'ما لا يدل جزوه على جزء معناه مفرد'. This is the key test.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المفرد: غير المركب وهو موضوع البحث. المصنف قسم اللفظ إلى مفرد وإلى مركب. وغايته من ذلك المفرد. فإنه يقسم إلى أقسام باعتبارات مختلفة؛ لأنه قد يقسم من حيث الدلالة إلى: العلم، والمتواطئ والمشكك، والمشترك، والمنقول، والحقيقة، والمجاز. ويقسم إلى كلي وجزئي. ومن حيث الاستقلال بالفهم وعدمه إلى الاسم والكلمة (الفعل) والأداة. ما يدل جزوه على جزء معناه مركب إسنادي من مسند ومسند إليه، مثل: الجامع واسع. إضافي: من مضاف ومضاف إليه مثل: قلم المدرس. تقييدي من صفة وموصوف مثل: عالم فاضل عندنا. تركيبي: يعني من كلمتين مثل: بعلبك. المستعمل. ما لا يدل جزؤه على جزء معناه مفرد. ينقسم إلى: ١ كلمة: وهو الفعل عند النحاة. ٢. اسم. أداة: وهي أعم من الحرف عند النحاة.
المفرد (simple) is that which is not مركب (compound), and it is the subject of investigation. The author divided the lafz into مفرد and مركب, and his goal in that is the مفرد. For it is divided into divisions according to various considerations: because it may be divided from the aspect of delalation (indication) into: علم (proper name), متواطئ (univocal), مشكك (equivocal in gradation), مشترك (homonymous), منقول (transferred), حقيقة (literal), and مجاز (metaphorical). And it is divided into كلي (universal) and جزئي (particular). And from the aspect of independence in understanding and its absence, into اسم (noun), كلمة (verb), and أداة (particle). As for what part of it indicates part of its meaning, it is مركب: إسنادي (predicative) like 'al-jami'u wasi'un' (the mosque is spacious); إضافي (annexation) like 'qalamu al-mudarrisi' (the teacher's pen); تقييدي (restrictive) like 'alimun fadilun' (a virtuous scholar) at us; تركيبي (compositional) meaning from two words like 'Ba'labakka' (Baalbek). Al-musta'mal (the used). As for what part of it does not indicate part of its meaning, it is مفرد. It is divided into: 1. كلمة (verb), which is the verb according to grammarians; 2. اسم (noun); 3. أداة (particle), which is more general than الحرف (letter/preposition) according to grammarians.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage provides the definition and exhaustive divisions of مفرد. The commentator begins by stating that مفرد is simply 'what is not مركب', and it is the main subject of logic. The author divided the lafz into مفرد and مركب, but his real concern is the مفرد because it is the building block of definitions and propositions. Then the commentator lists the divisions of مفرد according to three different considerations: (1) From the aspect of دلالة (indication): there are seven types: علم (proper name, like 'Muhammad'), متواطئ (univocal, applied equally to all individuals like 'human'), مشكك (equivocal in gradation, like 'existence' which applies to God and creatures in different degrees), مشترك (homonymous, like 'ayn meaning eye or spring), منقول (transferred, like 'salat' originally meaning prayer but later used for the ritual prayer), حقيقة (literal, used in its original meaning), and مجاز (metaphorical, used in a transferred sense). (2) From the aspect of universality: كلي (universal, like 'human' applying to many) and جزئي (particular, like 'Zayd' applying to one). (3) From the aspect of independence in understanding: اسم (noun which can stand alone in meaning), كلمة (verb, called 'kalima' here according to grammarians), and أداة (particle, which needs another word to complete meaning). Then the commentator turns to مركب and distinguishes two kinds: (a) مركب whose part indicates part of its meaning, like predicative compounds ('the mosque is spacious'), annexation compounds ('the teacher's pen'), restrictive compounds ('a virtuous scholar'), and compositional compounds ('Baalbek' which is a single word made of two originally separate words). (b) مركب whose part does not indicate part of its meaning, which is essentially the مفرد itself. Finally, he repeats the division of مفرد into verb, noun, and particle, noting that the term 'adatu' is more general than 'harf' in grammar. This is important for understanding the basic units of logical discourse.

Key Terms
المفرد
المركب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any word that has more than one letter
B) That which is not compound
C) That which indicates only one meaning
D) A word used in logic only

Key Takeaway
Mufrad is defined negatively as what is not compound, forming the basic unit of logical analysis.

Seven Types of Mufrad by Indication (Dalala)
Lists the seven types of mufrad by dalala

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the seven types of mufrad based on their mode of indication: 'alam, mutawati', mushakkik, mushtarak, manqul, haqiqa, majaz.

Core Idea
A single mufrad term indicates its meaning in seven distinct ways.

The logician classifies mufrad terms not only by structure but also by how they signify meaning. This lesson unpacks the seven types based on 'dalala' (indication), crucial for understanding definitions and avoiding ambiguity in religious texts.

Guided Path
1
Locate the seven types in the Arabic
Find the list: 'العلم، والمتواطئ والمشكك، والمشترك، والمنقول، والحقيقة، والمجاز'.
2
Understand each type's distinguishing feature
علم: proper name for a specific individual. متواطئ: univocal, applies equally to all individuals. مشكك: graded, applies differently (e.g., 'existence'). مشترك: homonymous, one word for multiple meanings. منقول: transferred, originally for one meaning then moved to another. حقيقة: literal usage. مجاز: metaphorical usage with a relation.
The commentary explains each briefly.
3
Apply to Islamic examples
For mutawati: 'insan' (human). For mushtarak: 'ayn' (eye/spring). For manqul: 'salat' (prayer). For haqiqa and majaz: 'asad' (lion) literal for the animal, metaphorical for a brave man.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage provides the definition and exhaustive divisions of مفرد. The commentator begins by stating that مفرد is simply 'what is not مركب', and it is the main subject of logic. The author divided the lafz into مفرد and مركب, but his real concern is the مفرد because it is the building block of definitions and propositions. Then the commentator lists the divisions of مفرد according to three different considerations: (1) From the aspect of دلالة (indication): there are seven types: علم (proper name, like 'Muhammad'), متواطئ (univocal, applied equally to all individuals like 'human'), مشكك (equivocal in gradation, like 'existence' which applies to God and creatures in different degrees), مشترك (homonymous, like 'ayn meaning eye or spring), منقول (transferred, like 'salat' originally meaning prayer but later used for the ritual prayer), حقيقة (literal, used in its original meaning), and مجاز (metaphorical, used in a transferred sense). (2) From the aspect of universality: كلي (universal, like 'human' applying to many) and جزئي (particular, like 'Zayd' applying to one). (3) From the aspect of independence in understanding: اسم (noun which can stand alone in meaning), كلمة (verb, called 'kalima' here according to grammarians), and أداة (particle, which needs another word to complete meaning). Then the commentator turns to مركب and distinguishes two kinds: (a) مركب whose part indicates part of its meaning, like predicative compounds ('the mosque is spacious'), annexation compounds ('the teacher's pen'), restrictive compounds ('a virtuous scholar'), and compositional compounds ('Baalbek' which is a single word made of two originally separate words). (b) مركب whose part does not indicate part of its meaning, which is essentially the مفرد itself. Finally, he repeats the division of مفرد into verb, noun, and particle, noting that the term 'adatu' is more general than 'harf' in grammar. This is important for understanding the basic units of logical discourse.

Key Terms

متواطئ
مشكك
مشترك
منقول
حقيقة
مجاز

Key Takeaway
Mufrad is divided into seven types by indication, each with a distinct mode of signification.

Mufrad by Universality and Independence; and Murakkab Types
Covers divisions by universality and independence, then murakkab types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify mufrad as kulli/juz'i and ism/kalima/adat, and also identify the four types of murakkab.

Core Idea
Mufrad can be universal or particular; noun, verb, or particle; and compounds are divided by how their parts contribute to meaning.

This lesson completes the classification of mufrad by looking at two other considerations: universality and independence of meaning. It also introduces the corresponding types of murakkab, which are essential for constructing propositions and definitions.

Guided Path
1
Recognise the division into kulli and juz'i
From the Arabic: 'ويقسم إلى كلي وجزئي'. A kulli applies to many (e.g., 'human'), a juz'i applies to one (e.g., 'Zayd').
2
Recognise the division into ism, kalima, adat
From the Arabic: 'إلى الاسم والكلمة (الفعل) والأداة'. Ism stands alone, kalima (verb) indicates time and needs subject, adat (particle) needs connection.
3
Identify the four types of murakkab
The passage lists: isnaadi (predicative like 'al-jami'u wasi'un'), idaafi (annexation like 'qalamu al-mudarrisi'), taqyidi (restrictive like 'alimun fadilun'), and tarkiibi (compositional like 'Ba'labakka').
Note that tarkiibi is a single word made of two original words.
4
Distinguish murakkab from mufrad
Use the test: 'ما لا يدل جزوه على جزء معناه مفرد' — if parts indicate part of the meaning, it is murakkab; otherwise mufrad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المفرد: غير المركب وهو موضوع البحث. المصنف قسم اللفظ إلى مفرد وإلى مركب. وغايته من ذلك المفرد. فإنه يقسم إلى أقسام باعتبارات مختلفة؛ لأنه قد يقسم من حيث الدلالة إلى: العلم، والمتواطئ والمشكك، والمشترك، والمنقول، والحقيقة، والمجاز. ويقسم إلى كلي وجزئي. ومن حيث الاستقلال بالفهم وعدمه إلى الاسم والكلمة (الفعل) والأداة. ما يدل جزوه على جزء معناه مركب إسنادي من مسند ومسند إليه، مثل: الجامع واسع. إضافي: من مضاف ومضاف إليه مثل: قلم المدرس. تقييدي من صفة وموصوف مثل: عالم فاضل عندنا. تركيبي: يعني من كلمتين مثل: بعلبك. المستعمل. ما لا يدل جزؤه على جزء معناه مفرد. ينقسم إلى: ١ كلمة: وهو الفعل عند النحاة. ٢. اسم. أداة: وهي أعم من الحرف عند النحاة.
المفرد (simple) is that which is not مركب (compound), and it is the subject of investigation. The author divided the lafz into مفرد and مركب, and his goal in that is the مفرد. For it is divided into divisions according to various considerations: because it may be divided from the aspect of delalation (indication) into: علم (proper name), متواطئ (univocal), مشكك (equivocal in gradation), مشترك (homonymous), منقول (transferred), حقيقة (literal), and مجاز (metaphorical). And it is divided into كلي (universal) and جزئي (particular). And from the aspect of independence in understanding and its absence, into اسم (noun), كلمة (verb), and أداة (particle). As for what part of it indicates part of its meaning, it is مركب: إسنادي (predicative) like 'al-jami'u wasi'un' (the mosque is spacious); إضافي (annexation) like 'qalamu al-mudarrisi' (the teacher's pen); تقييدي (restrictive) like 'alimun fadilun' (a virtuous scholar) at us; تركيبي (compositional) meaning from two words like 'Ba'labakka' (Baalbek). Al-musta'mal (the used). As for what part of it does not indicate part of its meaning, it is مفرد. It is divided into: 1. كلمة (verb), which is the verb according to grammarians; 2. اسم (noun); 3. أداة (particle), which is more general than الحرف (letter/preposition) according to grammarians.

The author divided the lafz into مفرد and مركب, but his real concern is the مفرد because it is the building block of definitions and propositions. Essential vs. Accidental Universals in Islamic Logic
Author defines essential and accidental universals with examples and addresses an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish essential universals from accidental universals and explain why species is considered essential despite being identical to the essence.

Core Idea
Essential universals define what something is; accidental universals describe what it does or has.

In Islamic logic, all universals are divided into two categories: essential (dhati) and accidental (aradi). This division is crucial for understanding definitions and classifications. The author defines each, provides examples, and addresses a subtle objection about calling the species itself 'essential' even though it is the essence itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Find the terms 'essential' (ذاتي) and 'accidental' (عرضي) in the Arabic text. Note their definitions: essential is what is not outside the essence; accidental is what differs from the essence.
2
Examine the examples
The author gives genus, differentia, and species as essential universals, and 'laughing' (الضاحك) for man as accidental. Consider why each is classified as such.
Essential universals are part of the quiddity; accidental are outside.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection states: if the species is identical to the essence, how can it be called essential? Understand the problem: calling it 'essential' seems redundant if it is the essence itself.
4
Understand the resolution
The author responds that the term 'essential' is used in a technical, terminological sense (اصطلاحي), not a real ontological sense. This means the classification is logical, not metaphysical.
This avoids confusion between logical and real composition.
5
Apply to a new example
Take 'animal' and 'walking' for man. Determine which is essential and which accidental, and explain your reasoning.
Animal is essential (genus); walking is accidental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ينقسم الكلي إلى ذاتي وعرضي. الذاتي هو ما ليس خارجاً عن الذات، كالجنس والفصل والنوع. وأما العرضي فهو الذي يخالف الذات، أي لا يدخل في حقيقة جزئياته بأحد المعنيين، كالضاحك بالنسبة إلى الإنسان فإنه خارج. فإن قلت: حقيقة النوع عين الذات، فكيف يكون ذاتيا؟ قلت: جوابه المشهور: إن إطلاق الذاتي عليه اصطلاحي لا حقيقي.
The universal is divided into essential and accidental. The essential is that which is not outside the essence, like genus, differentia, and species. As for the accidental, it is that which differs from the essence, i.e., does not enter into the reality of its particulars in either of the two senses, like 'laughing' with respect to man, for it is outside. If you say: The reality of the species is the essence itself, so how can it be essential? I say: Its well-known answer is that the application of 'essential' to it is terminological, not real.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage defines the two main divisions of the universal: essential (dhati) and accidental (aradi). Essential universals are those that are part of the quiddity of the thing, such as 'animal' as genus for man, 'rational' as differentia, and 'man' as species. Accidental universals are those that are outside the quiddity, such as 'laughing' for man; they do not constitute the essence. The text then anticipates an objection: if the species is identical to the essence, how can it be called 'essential'? The answer is that the term 'essential' here is used in a technical, terminological sense (istilahi), not in a literal sense meaning that it is a part. This clarifies that the classification is based on logical analysis, not on real ontological composition. The example of 'laughing' (al-dahik) is a common accidental universal for man, while 'rational' (al-natiq) is an essential differentia. This division is fundamental in Islamic logic for understanding definitions and classifications.

عرضي
كلي
حقيقة
اصطلاحي

Two Meanings of Dhat in Logical Discourse
Author clarifies the dual reference of 'dhat': essence vs instances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two meanings of 'dhat' (essence) in logical contexts and identify which meaning is intended in a given definition.

Core Idea
Dhat can refer to the abstract essence or to its concrete instances—context determines which.

The term 'dhat' is foundational in Islamic logic, especially in definitions (hadd). However, as the author clarifies, it has a dual reference that can cause confusion. This lesson unpacks that ambiguity and equips you to navigate it in any logical text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terminological ambiguity
Recognize that 'dhat' can mean either the essence itself (e.g., 'humanity') or the individuals it is true of (e.g., 'Zayd'). The author explicitly states both usages.
Early texts sometimes restrict 'dhat' to essence; here the second meaning is highlighted.
2
Locate contextual clues
Look for phrases like 'nask al-haqiqa' (the essence itself) vs. 'ma sadaqa 'alayhi al-haqiqa' (that which the essence is true of) to determine the intended sense.
If the text speaks of 'relating the essence to its instances', the second meaning is likely intended.
3
Apply to a definition
When encountering 'dhat' in a definition, check if the definiendum is an abstract concept or a concrete instance—this tells you which meaning is operative.
For example, in 'Man is a rational animal', 'man' refers to the essence, not an individual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لغوي، فلا يقتضي المغايَرَةَ بين المنسوب والمنسوب إلَيْهِ. وأقول: الذات كما يطلق على نفس الحقيقة يطلق على ما صدق عليه الحقيقة، فربما يراد بالذات ها هنا المعنى الثاني فيمكن نسبة نفس الحقيقة إلى ما صدق عليه الحقيقة كما يمكن نسبة جزئيها إليه.
Linguistically, it does not imply distinction between the relative and the related. And I say: the essence (dhat) is used for the essence itself and also for that which the essence is true of. Perhaps by 'essence' here the second meaning is intended, so the essence itself can be related to that which the essence is true of, just as its two parts can be related to it.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage clarifies a potential ambiguity in the term 'dhat' (essence). The author first notes that linguistically, the term does not necessitate a distinction between the entity being related and the entity it is related to. Then he explains that 'dhat' can be used in two ways: first, to refer to the essence itself (e.g., 'humanity'), and second, to refer to the concrete subjects that the essence is true of (e.g., Zayd or 'Amr as individuals). In the context under discussion, perhaps the second meaning is intended. This allows us to relate the essence to its instances, just as we can relate the parts of the essence (genus and differentia) to the essence itself. For example, we can say 'Humanity is true of Zayd' similarly to how we say 'Animality and rationality are parts of humanity.' This distinction is crucial in logical discussions about definitions and universal concepts.

Key Terms

Key Takeaway
The term 'dhat' in logic can refer either to the abstract essence or to the concrete individuals that instantiate it; context distinguishes.

Definition of Genus by Rasm: Why It Is Rasm Not Hadd
Author explains the rasm definition of genus and defends its status as rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of the rasm definition of genus and explain why it is classified as a rasm rather than a hadd.

Core Idea
The rasm of genus uses accidental properties, so it is not an essential definition.

In Islamic logic, definitions can be essential (hadd) or descriptive (rasm). This passage defines the genus (al-jins) by rasm: 'a universal predicated of many differing in realities in answer to what is it?'. The author unpacks each part and argues that because predicability is accidental to the genus, the definition is a rasm. Understanding this distinction is key to precise definition in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Extract the full rasm definition
Find the complete definition in the Arabic: 'كلي مقول على كثيرين مختلفين بالحقائق في جواب ما هو'. Write it out and identify each component.
2
Identify each component's role
For each phrase (كلي, مقول, على كثيرين, مختلفين بالحقائق, في جواب ما هو), note what it adds and what it excludes (ihtiraz). For example, 'مختلفين بالحقائق' excludes species which are predicated of many agreeing in reality.
The author considers specifying the precaution only to species as arbitrary (tahakkum).
3
Understand why predicability is accidental
The author states that the genus in itself is an essential universal regardless of whether it is actually predicated. Predicability is an accidental property that occurs after its constitution. This is the key reason the definition is a rasm.
Cite the reference to Sharh al-Isharat for support.
4
Distinguish hadd from rasm in this context
A hadd would use only essential constituents (genus and differentia). Since 'predicated of many' is an accident, the definition is a rasm. Practice by contrasting with a hypothetical hadd of genus (e.g., 'essential universal of things differing in reality').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُرْسَمُ : بأَنَّهُ كُلّيّ مقول على كثيرين مختلفين بالحقائق في جواب ما هو. فالكلي جنس للجنس، شامل لسائر الكليات. والمقولُ إنما ذكر ليتعلق به على كثيرين، فليس شيء منهما مستدركا . وإنما ذكر على كثيرين؛ ليوصف بقوله: مختلفين بالحقيقة. وقوله: مختلفين بالحقائقِ احتراز بذلك عن النوع والخاصة والفصل القريب. وتخصيص الاحتراز بالنوع تحكم وقوله في جواب ما هو احتراز عن الفصل البعيد، والعرض العام وخاصة الجنس. وإنما كان هذا وأمثاله رسماً؛ لأن المقولية عارضة للكليات والتعريف بالعارض رسم. وذلك؛ لأنَّ الجِنْسَ في نَفْسِه هو الكُلَّيُّ الذاتي لمختلفات الحقيقة سواء قيل عليها أو لم يقل. أما المقولية وكونه صالحا لها فمما يعرضُ له بعد تقومه، كذا في شرح الإشارات، فلا يلتفت إلى ما يقال : إنها حدود لكونها أموراً.
And it is defined by rasm: that it is a universal predicated of many differing in realities in answer to 'what is it?'. So 'universal' is a genus for genus, inclusive of all universals. And 'predicated' is mentioned only to attach to it 'of many', so neither of them is redundant. And it was mentioned 'of many' so that it may be described by his saying: differing in reality. And his saying: differing in realities is a precaution against species, peculiar property, and proximate differentia. And specifying the precaution to species is arbitrary. And his saying: 'in answer to what is it?' is a precaution against remote differentia, common accident, and the peculiar property of genus. And this and its like are only rasm because predicability is accidental to universals, and definition by accident is rasm. That is because the genus in itself is the essential universal of things differing in reality, whether it is predicated of them or not. As for predicability and being suitable for it, that is something that occurs to it after its constitution, as in Sharh al-Isharat, so no attention is paid to what is said: that they are definitions because they are matters.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage defines the genus (jins) by way of rasm (descriptive definition) and justifies why it is a rasm and not a hadd (essential definition). The author begins by stating the rasm of genus: 'a universal predicated of many differing in realities in answer to what is it?'. Then he unpacks each part. 'Universal' here is itself a genus for the term 'genus', as it includes all other universals (species, differentia, etc.). The term 'predicated' is not redundant; it is needed to attach the phrase 'of many'. The phrase 'of many' is included to allow the qualification 'differing in reality'. The author then explains the precautions (ihtirazat): 'differing in realities' excludes species (which are predicated of many agreeing in reality), peculiar property (khassa), and proximate differentia (fasl qarib). He criticizes the view that restricts the precaution to species as arbitrary (tahakkum). The phrase 'in answer to what is it?' excludes remote differentia (fasl ba'id), common accident ('arad 'amm), and the peculiar property of genus (khasat al-jins). The author then argues that this definition is a rasm, not a hadd, because predicability is an accident ('arad) of the genus. The genus in itself is an essential (dhati) universal that applies to things differing in reality, regardless of whether it is actually predicated. Predicability is an accidental property that occurs to it after its constitution (taqawwum). This is cited from Sharh al-Isharat of Ibn Sina. Therefore, one should not heed those who claim these definitions are hadd because they are essential matters.

Key Terms
رسم
جنس
كلي
مقول على كثيرين
حد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the definition of genus as 'a universal predicated of many differing in realities in answer to what is it?' considered a rasm rather than a hadd?
A) Because it uses the term 'universal' which is itself a genus.
B) Because predicability is an accidental property, not an essential constituent of genus.
C) Because the definition includes the phrase 'in answer to what is it?' which is only for species.
D) Because the genus is not really a universal.

Key Takeaway
The rasm definition of genus is a rasm because it uses an accidental property (predicability) rather than essential constituents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Why Definitions Using Predication Are Rasm
Author refutes a criticism and explains that predication is accidental, making definitions rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hadd and rasm by identifying whether a definition uses accidental properties like maquliyya.

Core Idea
A definition using accidental predication is rasm, not hadd.

In Islamic logic, a complete definition (hadd) must capture the essence of a thing using essential properties. But some definitions rely on accidental attributes like predication (maquliyya). This passage explains why such definitions are only descriptions (rasm) and why that matters for rigorous definitional work in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about maquliyya
The author argues that definitions using 'being predicated' (maquliyya) as a defining property are merely descriptions. Locate the statement in the Arabic where this claim is made.
The key phrase is 'لأن المقولية عارضة للكليات' (because maquliyya is accidental to universals).
2
Understand the nature of the genus in itself
The author states that the genus in itself (الجنس في نفسه) is an essential universal that applies to many things differing in reality, regardless of whether it is actually predicated. This is the essential core of the genus.
The genus does not require actual predication to be what it is.
3
Recognize that maquliyya is accidental
Predication and the suitability for predication occur after the genus is constituted. They are attributes that happen to the genus, not constitutive of its essence. Thus, they are accidental.
The author cites Sharh al-Isharat to support this: 'فمما يعرض له بعد تقومه' (it is something that occurs to it after its constitution).
4
Conclude that definitions using maquliyya are rasm
Since maquliyya is accidental, any definition that relies on it cannot be a true essential definition (hadd) but only a description (rasm). This is because a hadd must use only essential, constitutive properties.
The author dismisses the objection that such definitions are hadd because they deal with 'intentional matters' (أمور اعتبارية) – they are still rasm.
5
Apply the criterion to other definitions
The same principle applies whenever a definition uses an accidental property. Learn to spot such cases: if the defining property is not part of the essence but occurs after it, the definition is rasm.
This helps in evaluating definitions in fiqh, kalam, and other Islamic disciplines.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتخصيص الاحتراز بالنوع تحكم. وقوله في جواب ما هو احتراز عن الفصل البعيد، والعرض العام وخاصة الجنس. وإنما كان هذا وأمثاله رسماً؛ لأن المقولية عارضة للكليات والتعريف بالعارض رسم. وذلك؛ لأنَّ الجِنْسَ في نَفْسِه هو الكُلَّيُّ الذاتي لمختلفات الحقيقة سواء قيل عليها أو لم يقل. أما المقولية وكونه صالحا لها فمما يعرضُ له بعد تقومه، كذا في شرح الإشارات، فلا يلتفت إلى ما يقال : إنها حدود لكونها أموراً اعتبارية).
And specifying the exclusion to the type is arbitrary. And his statement 'in answer to 'what is it' is a safeguard against the distant differentia, the general accident, and the specific property of the genus.' And this and its likes are only description (rasm) because predication (maquliyya) is accidental to universals, and definition by accident is description. That is because the genus in itself is the essential universal of things differing in reality, whether it is predicated of them or not. As for predication and its being suitable for it, that is something that occurs to it after its constitution, as in Sharh al-Isharat. So no attention is paid to what is said: that they are definitions because they are intentional matters.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a critical explanation of why certain definitions are considered rasm (description) rather than hadd (strict definition). The author first identifies that the objection (that specifying the exclusion to a certain type is arbitrary) is invalid. Then he explains that the expression 'in answer to 'what is it'' is used to exclude the remote differentia, the general accident, and the specific property of the genus. Such definitions are rasm because they rely on predication (maquliyya), which is an accidental property of universals. The genus in itself is an essential universal that applies to things differing in reality, regardless of whether it is actually predicated. Predication and the suitability for predication are accidental attributes that come after the genus is established in itself. This is cited from Sharh al-Isharat. Therefore, the claim that such definitions are genuine definitions (hadd) because they involve intentional matters is to be disregarded.

Hadd vs Rasm: The Controversy Over Conventional Attributes
Author contrasts earlier and later logicians on definition criteria

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the positions of earlier and later logicians on whether definitions using conventional attributes (i'tibariyya) qualify as hadd or rasm.

Core Idea
Earlier logicians demanded real essences for hadd; later logicians accepted conventional ones.

The distinction between hadd (strict definition) and rasm (descriptive definition) depends on the ontological status of the attributes used. Earlier logicians insisted that only real components of the thing (dhatiyyat haqiqiyya) can constitute a hadd; conventional attributes (i'tibariyya), even if treated as essential in a discipline like grammar, yield only a rasm. Later logicians, however, collapsed this distinction: once a discipline considers an attribute essential, definitions using it become hadd within that discipline. This passage from Fanari's commentary illustrates the shift.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two schools
The passage distinguishes between 'mutaqaddimun' (earlier logicians) and 'muta'akhkhirun' (later logicians). Note what each group says about definitions: earlier require real components; later accept conventional ones.
These groups are not always explicitly named in other texts; here they are central.
2
Extract the criterion for hadd
For earlier logicians, a hadd must consist of real, natural components of the defined thing (dhatiyyat haqiqiyya). Anything less is a rasm. Identify what they consider 'real' – i.e., part of the thing's essence in external reality.
Real components are contrasted with 'i'tibariyya' (conventional).
3
Analyze the example: kalima
The passage uses 'kalima' (word) defined as 'qawl mufrad' (single utterance). Grammarians consider this essential, but earlier logicians note it is not a real constituent of a word in nature. Determine how each school classifies this definition.
In reality, a word has no 'singleness' as a component; it is a conventional classification.
4
Contrast the later position
Later logicians ignore the real/conventional distinction. They accept definitions like 'qawl mufrad' as hadd because grammarians have adopted them as essential. Understand: the status depends on disciplinary convention, not ontology.
This shift has practical implications: definitions in Islamic sciences become acceptable as hadd within those sciences.
5
Apply the distinction
Given a definition from an Islamic science (e.g., fiqh or usul al-fiqh), decide whether earlier or later logicians would accept it as hadd, and explain why.
Use the criteria: real vs. conventional components.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المتقدمون من المناطقة يرون التعريف بالذاتيات حداً، أي: المكوَّنُ منها المعرَّف في الواقع وخِلْقَة، وأيُّ أوصاف لم تكن من مكوناتِ الشيء خِلْقَةٌ تكون مكونات اعتبارية -أي اعتبرت من جهة مثل: الكلمة قول مفرد، فإن النحاة اعتبروها ذاتيات للكلمة وليست في واقع الأمر، فقال المتقدمون من المناطقة: التعريف بها يكون رسما لا حداً. أما المتأخرون فإنهم لم يفرقوا بين الأوصاف الذاتية والاعتبارية؛ لذلك يرون التعريف بها حداً؛ لأنها بعد أن اعتبرها النحاة أن (قول مفرد) هي ذاتيات الكلمة صار التعريف بها حداً.
The earlier logicians hold that definition by essential properties (dhatiyyat) is a strict definition (hadd), meaning that the defined is composed of them in reality and nature. Any descriptions that are not among the components of the thing in nature are conventional components (i'tibariyya) – that is, considered from a certain perspective, such as the word (kalima) being 'a single utterance' (qawl mufrad). The grammarians consider it essential to the word, but in reality it is not. So the earlier logicians say: definition by them is description (rasm), not a strict definition. As for the later logicians, they did not distinguish between essential and conventional attributes; therefore they consider definition by them a strict definition, because after the grammarians consider 'a single utterance' essential to the word, the definition by them becomes a strict definition.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a historical and theoretical clarification about the criteria for a definition being a hadd (strict definition) versus a rasm (description). The author explains that earlier logicians (mutaqaddimun) insisted that a hadd must consist of real essences (dhatiyyat haqiqiyya) – that is, components that actually constitute the thing in external reality and nature. If a description does not belong to the real constituents but is considered essential by convention (i'tibari), such as the grammarians considering 'a single utterance' to be an essential property of 'word' (kalima), then that description is merely conventional. For the earlier logicians, definitions using such conventional attributes are rasm, not hadd. In contrast, later logicians (muta'akhkhirun) did not differentiate between real and conventional essential properties. According to them, once a discipline (e.g., grammar) considers a certain attribute as essential (like 'single utterance' for word), then definitions employing that attribute qualify as hadd within that discipline. Thus, the difference hinges on the ontological status of the components: real vs. conventional, and whether that matters for the definition's classification.

المتأخرون (muta'akhkhirun)

رسم (rasm)

B) Because grammarians do not consider it essential.
C) Because it includes the genus but not the differentia.
D) Because it is not convertible with the defined.

Key Takeaway
The classification of a definition as hadd or rasm depends on whether its components are real essences or conventional attributes, and later logicians accepted conventional attributes as sufficient within a discipline.

Early vs Late Logicians on Definition by Essential Attributes
Compares early and late logicians on whether definitions using essential or accidental attributes constitute hadd or rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the early and later logicians' views on what constitutes a hadd (real definition) and identify when a definition using conventional attributes qualifies as hadd or rasm.

Core Idea
For early logicians, hadd requires real essence; later logicians accept conventional essentiality.

In this passage, al-Fanari explains a key development in the science of definition. You will see how the criterion for a real definition (hadd) shifted from requiring actually constitutive attributes to accepting attributes that are merely considered essential by a particular discipline. The example of defining 'word' (kalima) as 'single utterance' illustrates the divide between early and late logicians.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate the claim of early logicians and the counterclaim of later logicians. Note the key terms: dhatiyyat (essential) vs i'tibariyya (conventional/accidental).
2
Examine the example of kalima
The definition 'word is a single utterance' is given. Understand why early logicians say it is a rasm, while later say it is a hadd.
3
Determine the criterion shift
What changed? Early: only real constitution. Later: conventional acceptance by the relevant science (here, grammar) is sufficient.
4
Apply the distinction to a new case
Given a definition like 'man is a rational animal', classify according to both views. Early logicians would say it is a hadd because rationality is constitutive; later logicians would also accept it as hadd.
This example uses the Islamic concept of man (insan) from kalam and usul.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱) المتقدمون من المناطقة يرون التعريف بالذاتيات حداً، أي: المكوَّنُ منها المعرَّف في الواقع وخِلْقَة، وأيُّ أوصاف لم تكن من مكوناتِ الشيء خِلْقَةٌ تكون مكونات اعتبارية -أي اعتبرت من جهة مثل: الكلمة قول مفرد، فإن النحاة اعتبروها ذاتيات للكلمة وليست في واقع الأمر، فقال المتقدمون من المناطقة: التعريف بها يكون رسما لا حداً. أما المتأخرون فإنهم لم يفرقوا بين الأوصاف الذاتية والاعتبارية؛ لذلك يرون التعريف بها حداً؛ لأنها بعد أن اعتبرها النحاة أن (قول مفرد) هي ذاتيات الكلمة صار التعريف بها حداً.
(1) The early logicians hold that definition by essential attributes is a hadd (real definition), i.e., composed of what constitutes the defined in reality and creation. Any attributes that were not part of the thing's constitution in creation are accidental components—i.e., considered from a certain perspective, like the word 'kalima' (word) is 'a single utterance', for the grammarians considered it essential for the word even though in reality it is not. So the early logicians said: defining by them is a rasm (description), not a hadd. As for the later logicians, they did not distinguish between essential and accidental attributes; therefore they consider definition by them a hadd, because after the grammarians considered that 'single utterance' is essential to the word, definition by them becomes a hadd.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage discusses a key difference between early and late logicians regarding the nature of definition (hadd vs rasm). The early logicians maintain that a true definition (hadd) must consist of attributes that are essential (dhatiyyat) to the thing in reality—that is, the attributes that constitute the thing's actual essence. If the attributes used are not actually constitutive but are merely considered as such from a conventional perspective (like grammarians treating 'single utterance' as essential to 'word'), then defining by them yields only a rasm (description), not a hadd. The late logicians, however, do not differentiate between essential and conventional attributes; they accept any set of attributes that are conventionally taken as essential as sufficient for a hadd. The example given is the definition of 'word' as 'single utterance': grammarians treat this as essential, so for the late logicians it qualifies as a hadd. The passage thus highlights a shift in the criteria for real definitions within the logical tradition.

The Objection and Response on Defining Genus by Universal
Objection and response on defining genus by universal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the valid and invalid aspects of using a specific property as a definiens in a definition by analyzing the objection and response regarding the definition of genus.

Core Idea
A definiens must be broader in concept, even if it is a specific property in another respect.

This passage presents a classic objection in definition theory: defining a general term like 'genus' using 'universal' seems to violate the rule that the definiens must be broader than the definiendum. But the response shows the rule is not absolute—it depends on which aspect of the definiens is considered. By understanding this dialectic, you will gain precision in evaluating definitions, a crucial skill in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find the objection: 'If you say: Genus of genus is more specific than absolute genus, and it is not permissible to define the general by one of its specific properties.' Note the condition being invoked: definiens must be broader.
2
Understand the basis of the objection
The objector argues that 'universal' is a specific property of 'genus' (since genus is a type of universal), so using 'universal' to define 'genus' violates the condition. Note that 'universal' is indeed one specific kind of universal.
3
Analyze the response
The responder distinguishes two aspects: (1) by its concept (mafhum), 'universal' is broader than 'genus' (since universal includes genus, species, differentia, etc.) – so it can be a valid definiens. (2) by consideration of an accident (being the genus of genus), it becomes specific. The objection only holds if we conflate the two aspects.
The response uses the example of 'animal' defined as 'moving man' to show the absurdity of the objection if taken absolutely.
4
Apply the principle to an Islamic example
Consider defining 'wine' (khamr) as 'intoxicating liquid'. 'Liquid' is broader than 'intoxicating liquid', so it's a valid genus. But if we said 'wine is intoxicating', that's a property, not a genus. Similarly, 'universal' is broader than 'genus' when considered as a concept, but if we treat it as a specific property, it fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إيراد على تعريف الجنس
(۱)
فإنْ قُلتَ جنس الجنس ) أخصُّ من مطلقِ الجِنْسِ، ولا يَجُوزُ تعريف العام بأحدِ خواصه.
قلتُ: إن أريدَ عَدَمُ الجواز عند اتحادِ اعتباري معرفيته و خصوصيَّتِهِ فَمُسلَّم، لكنَّه غيرُ مُفيد. وإِنْ أريد مطلقا فممنوع. وذلك؛ لأنَّ (٢) الكليّ بمَفْهومِهِ (٣) مُعَرِّفٌ وأَعَمُّ من مُطلَق الجِنْسِ وباعتبار عارض هو كونه جنساً للجِنْسِ أَخَصُّ مِنْهُ وغيرُ معرّفٍ (١) التعريف ينبغي أن يشتمل على جنس، وفصل أو جنس وعرض خاص، أو عرض عام، مثل: الإنسان حيوان ناطق أو ضاحك أو متنفس. وهنا عرف الجنس وجعل كلمة (كلي) جنساً له. والمعرَّفُ وهو لفظ (الجنس) المعرَّف يشمل جميع الأجناس المعرَّف بها، وكلمة (كلي) في تعريف الجنس أحد أفراد الجنس العام؛ إذ هو أخص من الجنس. ومن شروط المعرّف أن يكون أعم من المعرَّف، وهنا عرفنا العام ببعض خواصه. (٢) الجواب إنْ قال: لا يجوز هذا التعريف عند ملاحظة كونه جزءاً من التعريف مع خصوصيته بالنسبة لمطلق الجنس المعرَّفِ، فإنا نسلم عدمَ الجواز؛ لأنه تعريف للعام ببعض جزئياته (أفراده) وإنّه غير مفيد للتعريف كما نقول: الحيوان إنسان متحرك.
Objection regarding the definition of genus
(1) If you say: 'Genus of genus is more specific than absolute genus, and it is not permissible to define the general by one of its specific properties.'
I say: If what is meant is the impermissibility when the aspect of its being a definer and its specificity are united, then it is granted, but it is not useful. If it is meant absolutely, then it is prevented. That is because (2) the universal by its concept is a definer and more general than absolute genus, but by consideration of an accident which is its being a genus for genus, it is more specific than it and not a definer. (1) A definition should contain a genus and a differentia, or a genus and a specific property, or a general property, like: man is a rational animal, or laughing, or breathing. Here he defined genus and made the word 'universal' its genus. The definiendum, which is the word 'genus' defined, encompasses all genera that are defined by it, and the word 'universal' in the definition of genus is one of the individuals of the universal genus; as it is more specific than genus. And one of the conditions of the definiens is that it be more general than the definiendum, and here we defined the general by some of its specific properties. (2) The answer: If he says: this definition is not permissible when considering its being a part of the definition with its specificity relative to the absolute genus being defined, then we concede its impermissibility; because it is a definition of the general by some of its particulars (individuals), and it is not useful for definition, as we say: 'animal is a moving man.'
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents a typical dialectical objection (irad) and response (jawab) regarding the definition of 'genus' (jins). The objection states that the definition of genus as 'a universal predicated of many things differing in species' (implicitly) uses 'universal' as the genus, but 'universal' is actually a specific property of genus (since genus is a type of universal). Therefore, defining the general term 'genus' by a specific property 'universal' violates the condition that the definiens must be broader than the definiendum. The response distinguishes between two aspects: In terms of its concept, 'universal' is indeed broader than 'genus' (since universal includes species, differentia, etc.), so it can serve as a definiens. However, if one considers the accidental aspect of 'universal' being specifically the genus of genus (i.e., the universal that is genus), it becomes narrower. The objection only holds if we consider both the definiens aspect and the specificity together, but that is not useful. The commentary then explains the conditions of definition, and reiterates the answer: the definition is invalid only if we consider the definiens as both a part of the definition and specific relative to the definiendum, but then it would be like defining 'animal' as 'moving man', which is clearly not a proper definition. Thus, the passage resolves the objection by clarifying the scope of the terms.

Key Terms
جنس
كلي
معرِّف
عارض

B) Because 'universal' is a synonym for 'genus' in the definition.

D) Because the definiendum 'genus' is not a general term.

Key Takeaway
A definiens is valid if it is broader in its essential concept, even if it is a specific property in an accidental aspect.

The Objection: Defining General by Specific is Invalid
Author presents an objection and the beginning of his reply.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical error of defining a general term by one of its specific subcategories and state the condition under which this rule applies.

Core Idea
Defining the general by a specific violates the coextensiveness requirement of definitions.

In this passage, an objector challenges the definition of genus as universal by invoking a key rule: the general cannot be defined by a specific. Let's unpack the objection and understand why it appears to be a problem.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and the proposed definiens
The definiendum is 'genus' (jins) and the proposed definiens is 'universal' (kulli). The objector claims that 'universal' in one sense is more specific than 'genus' (specifically, jins al-jins is more specific than mutlaq al-jins).
2
Extract the objection's claim
The objector says: 'It is not permissible to define the general by one of its specifics.' In other words, if the definiens is a specific under the definiendum, the definition is circular (the part is used to define the whole).
3
Determine the condition for the rule
The rule 'no defining general by specific' applies only when the definiens and definiendum are considered under the same respect (i'tibar). If the respects differ, the rule may not hold.
The author later clarifies this condition.
4
Apply the rule to the given definition
The objector assumes that 'universal' is always a specific of 'genus', thus the definition is invalid. But is that assumption correct under every respect?
This sets up the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفوائد الفنارية
إيراد على تعريف الجنس
(۱)
فإنْ قُلتَ جنس الجنس أخصُّ من مطلقِ الجِنْسِ، ولا يَجُوزُ تعريف العام بأحدِ خواصه.
قلتُ: إن أريدَ عَدَمُ الجواز عند اتحادِ اعتباري معرفيته و خصوصيَّتِهِ فَمُسلَّم، لكنَّه غيرُ مُفيد.
وإِنْ أريد مطلقا فممنوع.
وذلك؛ لأنَّ
(۲)
الكليّ بمَفْهومِهِ مُعَرِّفٌ وأَعَمُّ من مُطلَق الجِنْسِ
وباعتبار عارض هو كونه جنساً للجِنْسِ أَخَصُّ مِنْهُ وغيرُ معرّفٍ
فالأمرانِ جائزان في شيءٍ واحد بالاعتبارَيْن المُتغايرين.
وهو ما لا يمنع نفس تصوره من وقوع الشركة فيه، فإنه يصلح أن يكون جزءاً من التعريف، فإنه بهذا الاعتبار أعم من مطلق الجنس؛ لأنه يشمل الجنس والفصل والخاصة والعرض العام وباعتبار عارض هو كونه جنساً للجنس فهو أخص من مطلق الجنس فلا يصلح للتعريف به. إذن للفظ (كلي) نظرتان باعتباره كليا لا يمنع دخول الفصل والنوع، والخاصة والعرض العام، فإنه بهذا الاعتبار يعرفُ به وباعتبار کونه جنساً للجنس، فهو فرد من أفراد المعرّف فلا يعرف به.
The Fawaid al-Fanariyya
Objection to the Definition of Genus
(1)
If you say: 'The genus of genus is more specific than absolute genus, and it is not permissible to define the general by one of its specifics.'
I say: 'If what is meant is the impermissibility when there is unity of the two considerations of its being definitive and its being specific, then it is granted, but it is not useful. And if what is meant absolutely, then it is denied.'
That is because
(2)
The universal by its concept is definitive and more general than absolute genus, and by consideration of an accident which is its being a genus for the genus, it is more specific than it and not definitive.
So the two matters are permissible in one thing by the two differing considerations.
And it is that which does not prevent, in its own conception, the occurrence of sharing (commonality) in it, for it is fit to be a part of the definition, for in this respect it is more general than absolute genus because it encompasses genus, differentia, property, and common accident; and by consideration of an accident which is its being a genus for the genus, it is more specific than absolute genus, so it is not fit to be defined by it. Thus the expression 'universal' has two aspects: by its being a universal that does not prevent the entrance of differentia, species, property, and common accident, in this respect it is defined by it; and by consideration of its being a genus for the genus, it is an individual of the defined (individuals of the definiendum) and is not defined by it.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange (objection and answer) typical of the later commentary tradition in Islamic logic. The author presents a criticism against the definition of 'genus' (jins) as 'general' (kulli) and then refutes it by distinguishing two respects (i'tibaran). The objection states that 'jins al-jins' (genus of genus) is more specific (akhass) than 'mutlaq al-jins' (absolute genus), and it is not permissible to define the general (the definiendum) by one of its specifics (khawass). The author responds: if you mean impermissibility when there is unity of the two considerations (i.e., the same term considered both as a definitional part and as a specific), then conceded but not useful; if you mean absolutely, then denied. The reason is that the universal (kulli) in its concept (bi-mafhumihi) is a definer (mu'arif) and more general than absolute genus, but by virtue of an accident (bi-i'tibar 'arid) – its being a genus for genus – it is more specific and not a definer. Thus both judgments are permissible on the same thing but under different respects. The author further explains that 'universal' in its essence does not prevent commonality (sharika), so it is fit to be part of a definition; in that respect it is more general than absolute genus (because it includes genus, differentia, property, etc.). But considered as 'genus of genus,' it is a specific individual under the definiendum (absolute genus) and thus cannot define it. This illustrates a key logical principle: a term can be general in one sense and specific in another, resolving apparent contradictions. All examples used (genus, differentia, property, common accident) are from the standard logical classification of universals, relevant to definitions in the Islamic sciences such as defining 'insan' as 'hayawan natiq'.

Key Terms
جنس
كلّي
خاصة
عارض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the objection in this passage, what is the problem with defining 'genus' (jins) as 'universal' (kulli)?
A) The universal is too general and includes things that are not genus.
B) The universal is more specific than absolute genus, so it would be defining the general by a specific.
C) The universal is not a real definition because it lacks differentia.
D) The universal is a genus itself, causing circularity.

Key Takeaway
A definition must not define a general term by a specific subcategory under the same respect; the objection highlights this rule, but its application depends on the unity of respects.

The Refutation: Distinguishing Respects (I'tibarayn)
Author explains the distinction of respects to refute the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the distinction of respects (i'tibarayn) to resolve apparent contradictions in definitions and other logical statements.

Core Idea
The same term can be general under one respect and specific under another, resolving the paradox.

In the previous lesson, we saw the objection. Now the author refutes it by introducing a powerful logical tool: the distinction of respects (i'tibar). The universal is general in its essence but specific when considered as a genus of genus. This resolves the objection and shows the definition is sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two respects
The first respect is the universal's concept (mafhum) – its essence as 'that which does not prevent commonality'. The second is an accidental attribute ('arid) – its being a genus for genus (jins al-jins).
2
Determine the generality in each respect
In the first respect, the universal is more general than absolute genus because it includes genus, differentia, property, and common accident. In the second respect, it is more specific because it is a subset of absolute genus.
3
See how this refutes the objection
The objector assumed the universal is always specific, but the author shows it is only specific under one respect; under the respect relevant for definition (the concept), it is more general and thus a valid definiens.
4
Generalize the principle
The principle is: a single thing can have multiple attributes that place it at different levels of generality; one must specify the respect when evaluating definitions or arguments.

Source Text

Two Considerations of the Universal in Definition
Author explains two considerations of universal term for definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two considerations of a universal (kulli) and determine which is suitable for definition.

Core Idea
A universal can be used in definition only when it includes species, not when it is a genus of a genus.

The author of this passage analyzes the universal term 'kulli' from two angles. In the first consideration, it includes not only genus but also differentia, species, property, and common accident, making it broader than absolute genus and thus suitable as a part of definition. In the second consideration, it is taken as a genus of a genus, which is a specific instance under the definiendum and therefore cannot be used to define. Understanding this distinction is essential for constructing correct logical definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term 'kulli' and its dual role
The author states that the same term 'kulli' can be viewed in two ways. Locate the Arabic phrase 'للفظ كلي نظرتان' and note that it introduces two considerations.
The term 'kulli' is the universal itself.
2
Analyze the first consideration
The first consideration is 'كليا لا يمنع دخول الفصل والنوع، والخاصة والعرض العام'. That is, a universal that does not prevent the inclusion of differentia, species, property, and common accident. The author says it is 'أعم من مطلق الجنس' (more general than absolute genus) and 'يصلح أن يكون جزءاً من التعريف' (suitable to be a part of definition).
This consideration includes everything below the genus.
3
Analyze the second consideration
The second consideration is 'كونه جنساً للجنس' (being a genus of a genus). Under this aspect, the universal is 'أخص من مطلق الجنس' (more specific than absolute genus) and 'فرد من أفراد المعرّف' (an individual of the definiendum), so it cannot be used in definition.
Here the universal is subordinate to another genus.
4
Apply the distinction to a practical example
Given a term, decide whether it is used as a universal that includes species (first consideration) or as a genus of a genus (second). Only the first is suitable for defining something higher.
Practice with terms from fiqh, e.g., 'mal' (property).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالأمران جائزان في شيء واحد بالاعتبارين المتغايرين. وهو ما لا يمنع نفس تصوره من وقوع الشركة فيه، فإنه يصلح أن يكون جزءاً من التعريف، فإنه بهذا الاعتبار أعم من مطلق الجنس؛ لأنه يشمل الجنس والفصل والخاصة والعرض العام وباعتبار عارض هو كونه جنساً للجنس فهو أخص من مطلق الجنس فلا يصلح للتعريف به. إذن للفظ كلي نظرتان باعتباره كليا لا يمنع دخول الفصل والنوع، والخاصة والعرض العام، فإنه بهذا الاعتبار يعرف به وباعتبار كونه جنساً للجنس، فهو فرد من أفراد المعرّف فلا يعرف به.
The two matters are permissible in one thing by two different considerations. It is that whose mental conception does not prevent sharing in it, so it is suitable to be part of the definition. In this consideration it is more general than absolute genus because it includes genus, differentia, property, and common accident. By the consideration of an accident, namely being a genus of a genus, it is more specific than absolute genus and is not suitable for definition. Thus the expression 'kulli' has two considerations: by its being a universal that does not prevent the inclusion of differentia, species, property, and common accident—in this consideration it is used to define; and by its being a genus of a genus it is an individual of the definiendum and is not used to define.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage explains that a universal term like 'kulli' can be viewed in two ways. In the first consideration, it is a universal that can include species, differentiae, properties, and common accidents, making it broader than genus and suitable as a part of a definition. In the second consideration, it is taken as a genus of a genus, which is a specific individual under the definiendum, thus it cannot be used in a definition because it would be circular. The point is to distinguish between the universal in its absolute sense and the universal as a specific genus.

جنس

C) Because it is more general than absolute genus.
D) Because it includes differentia.

Key Takeaway
The universal term has two considerations: one includes species and is suitable for definition, the other is a genus of a genus and is not suitable.

What is a species? Definition and description of al-naw'
Author defines species as a universal predicated in answer to 'what is it?' covering individuals differing in number but sharing essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the species (النوع) from its description, apply it to Islamic examples, and distinguish it from genus and accident.

Core Idea
Species is a universal that tells the complete essence of its individuals, even when they differ in accidents.

This passage defines one of the five universals: species (النوع). It shows how species can answer 'what is it?' for both one individual and many. We will learn to recognize the key components of this definition and use it in logical analysis.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition
Find the phrase in the Arabic that defines species. It starts with 'ويرسم بأنه' (and it is described as). Write down the full description.
2
Identify the components
Break the description into parts: the genus (كلي) and the differentia (مقول على كثيرين مختلفين بالعدد دون الحقيقة في جواب ما هو؟). Understand each term.
The genus here is 'universal', not a substantial genus, indicating this is a rasm (description) rather than a hadd (definition).
3
Apply the example
Why is 'human' (الإنسان) a species? Check that it is said of both Zayd and Amr in answer to 'what is it?' and that it expresses their complete essence (تمام الحقيقة).
Notice that Zayd and Amr differ in accidents (color, height) but share the same essential reality.
4
Compare with genus
How does species differ from genus? Genus is also a universal in answer to 'what is it?' but applies to many species differing in essence. Species applies to individuals differing in number only.
The passage contrasts species with genus earlier: species involves both community (شركة) and particularity (خصوصية) together.
5
Classify the definition
The author says 'يرسم' (it is described). Determine whether this is a hadd (essential definition) or rasm (description). Since it uses a broad category ('universal') rather than a true genus, it is a rasm.
A rasm is still useful for distinguishing species from other universals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإما مقول في جواب ما هو؟ بحسب الشركة والخصوصية معا، كالإنسان بالنسبة إلى زيد وعمرو. أي يكون جوابا عن السؤال عن فرد خاص، وعن فردين، فإن الإنسان جواب لقولنا ما زيد؟ ولقولنا ما زيد وعمرو؛ لأنه تمام الحقيقة لكل فرد من أفراده المختلفة بالعوارض. وهو أي ذلك المقول النوع ويرسم بأنه كلي مقول على كثيرين مختلفين بالعدد دون الحقيقة في جواب ما هو؟
And sometimes it [the predicated] is said in answer to 'what is it?' according to community and particularity together, like 'human' in relation to Zayd and Amr. That is, it is an answer to the question about a particular individual and about two individuals: for 'human' is an answer to our saying 'What is Zayd?' and to our saying 'What are Zayd and Amr?' because it is the complete reality for every individual among its individuals differing by accidents. And that [predicated] is the species, and it is described as a universal predicated of many differing in number but not in reality in answer to 'what is it?'
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage defines the species (النوع). It begins by explaining that species is a term that can be used to answer the question 'What is it?' both for a single individual (like Zayd) and for multiple individuals (like Zayd and Amr). The example is 'human' (الإنسان) which applies to both Zayd and Amr because it expresses their complete essence (تمام الحقيقة), even though they differ in accidental attributes like color or height. The author then gives the technical description (رسم) of species: it is a universal predicated of many individuals that differ in number (i.e., are distinct individuals) but share the same essential reality (الحقيقة). This contrasts with genus, which applies to multiple species differing in essence, and with individual accidents, which are not predictable of many.

Key Terms
نوع
كلي
حقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is 'human' a valid answer to both 'What is Zayd?' and 'What are Zayd and Amr?'
A) Because Zayd and Amr have the same accidental attributes.
B) Because 'human' expresses the complete essence common to both.
C) Because 'human' is a genus that includes many species.
D) Because Zayd and Amr are the same individual.

Key Takeaway
Species is a universal that tells the complete essence of individuals, answering 'what is it?' for one or many, and differs from genus by not differing in essence.

Understanding the Definition of Species
Commentator explains the definition of species and its exclusions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each component of the definition of species and state which of the five universals it excludes.

Core Idea
The definition of species is a precise formula that excludes genus, differentia, property, and accident.

The commentator unpacks the definition of species phrase by phrase, showing how 'universal said of many differing in number without differing in reality' and 'in answer to what is it' serve to exclude other universals. Let's dissect this definition step by step.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the definiendum and the start of the definition
The baseline definition of species (naw') is: 'a universal said of many differing in number without differing in reality, in answer to what is it in its essence.' Locate this core in the Arabic.
The commentator begins by asserting that 'universal' and 'said of many' are not redundant.
2
2. Break down the definition into its component phrases
List the key phrases: (a) universal, (b) said of many, (c) differing in number without differing in reality, (d) in answer to what is it. Each phrase serves a logical function.
These phrases are not arbitrary; they systematically exclude other universals.
3
3. Map each phrase to the universal it excludes
- 'Without differing in reality' excludes genus, property of genus, common accident, and remote differentia (they involve real differences). - 'In answer to what is it' excludes proximate differentia and property of species (they answer 'which thing is it'). Use the commentary to confirm.
The commentator notes that specifying only genus is arbitrary; the exclusion is broader.
4
4. Verify the completeness of the exclusion
Check if any universal is not excluded. The five universals are: genus, species, differentia, property, common accident. The definition excludes all except species itself. Confirm by listing what remains.
The definition is designed to uniquely capture species.

فَذِكْرُ الكُليّ والمَقُولِ على كثيرين ليس بمُسْتَدْرَك كما مرّ، وقوله مختلفين بالعدَدِ دون الحقيقة: احتراز عن الجنس، وخاصته، والعرض العام، والفصل البعيد. وتخْصِيصُهُ بالاحتراز عن الجِنْسِ تحكُم. وقوله في جَوابِ ما هُوَ احتراز عن الفَصْلِ القَريبِ، وخاصة النوع فإنهما مَقُولانِ في جوابِ أَيُّ شَيْءٍ هو فِي ذَاتِهِ أَوْ فِي عَرْضِهِ. إيراد على قوله كثيرين: فإن قلت: الجنس وأمثاله يقال على كثيرين مختلفين في العدد أيضاً، كالحيوان في جواب ما زيد وعمرو وهذا الفرس وذلك الفرس فكيف يُحترز عنهما؟ قلت: هذا إن ورد فإنما يرد على من يحترز عنهما بوصف الكثيرين بالمتفقين بالحقيقة. أما ها هنا فلما نفي الاختلاف بالحقيقة بقوله: دون الحقيقة - صح الاحتراز عنهما: لأن الحيوان مثلاً لا يصح أن يقع جواباً إلا إذا اشتمل السؤال على مختلفين بالحقيقة، وإن اشتمل معها على المتفقين أيضاً.
The mention of 'universal' and 'said of many' is not redundant, as has passed. His saying 'differing in number without in reality' is a precaution against genus, its property, the common accident, and the remote differentia. And his specification of the precaution against genus is arbitrary. His saying 'in answer to 'what is it?' is a precaution against the proximate differentia and the property of the species, for they are said in answer to 'what is it?' in its essence or in its accident. An objection concerning his saying 'many': For if you say: Genus and its examples are said of many differing in number also, like 'animal' in answer to 'what is Zayd and 'Amr?' and 'this horse and that horse' — so how is one to be precautioned against them? I say: This, if it occurs, only occurs against one who takes precaution against them by describing the many as 'agreeing in reality'. As for here, since he negated difference in reality by his saying 'without reality', the precaution against them is correct: because 'animal', for example, is not valid to occur as an answer unless the question includes things differing in reality, even if it also includes things agreeing in reality.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of species (نوع) as 'a universal said of many differing in number without differing in reality'. The author first asserts that mentioning both 'universal' and 'said of many' is not redundant, as it covers all five universals. He then explains each part of the definition: 'differing in number without differing in reality' excludes genus, property of genus, common accident, and remote differentia. He criticizes specifying only genus as arbitrary. Next, 'in answer to 'what is it?' excludes proximate differentia and property of species, as these answer 'what is it' in essence or accident. An objection is raised: genus (e.g., 'animal') is also said of many differing in number, like when answering 'what is Zayd?' and 'what is this horse?' So how does the definition exclude genus? The answer distinguishes: the definition says 'without differing in reality', so if the question includes things differing in reality (like man and horse), genus applies; but if all are same species (like Zayd and 'Amr), genus applies too, but the definition's phrase 'without differing in reality' ensures that when the answer is uniform in reality, genus is not considered as an answer to 'what is it?' in the sense of species. Thus the precaution is valid.

خاصة

Key Takeaway
The definition of species is a precise tool that uses multiple phrases to systematically exclude all other universals, ensuring it captures only the species itself.

Resolving the Objection About Genus
Commentator responds to an objection about genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the objection against the definition of species and explain how the commentator defends it using the phrase 'without differing in reality'.

Core Idea
The phrase 'without differing in reality' is the key to excluding genus, because genus requires real difference among its instances.

An objector challenges that genus also applies to many differing in number, just like species. The commentator responds by showing that the definition's phrase 'without differing in reality' ensures that genus is excluded because genus applies only when the instances differ in reality. Let's analyze this logical defense.

Guided Path
1
1. State the objection in your own words
The objector says: Genus (e.g., 'animal') is said of many differing in number (Zayd, Amr, horse). So how does the definition exclude genus? It seems to include it.
The objection targets the phrase 'said of many differing in number'.
2
2. Identify the key defensive phrase
The commentator points to 'without differing in reality' as the crucial part. Find this phrase in the Arabic and notice how it modifies 'differing in number'.
The definition does not just say 'differing in number'; it adds 'without differing in reality'.
3
3. Understand the commentator's reasoning
He argues: Genus is only predicated when the things differ in reality (e.g., man and horse). If the things agree in reality (e.g., Zayd and Amr, both human), genus is not properly the answer; species is. So the phrase 'without differing in reality' excludes genus because genus requires real difference.
The objection fails because it ignores the full definition.
4
4. Apply the same logic to other examples
Test with a new example: 'Rational' is a differentia, not species. Does the definition exclude it? Yes, because differentia answers 'which thing is it?', not 'what is it?'.
The same structure works for all exclusions.

Defending the Definition of Species: Genus vs. Number
Author addresses an objection that genus, like animal, is said of many differing in number, and refutes it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the genus being said of many differing in number does not invalidate the definition of species as said of many differing in number without essence.

Core Idea
Genus and species differ in essence, not just in number.

In this passage, the author presents an objection against the standard definition of species and then refutes it. The objection confuses two types of multiplicity: differing in number and differing in essence. By grasping this distinction, you will see how the definition of species remains exclusive and precise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objector's claim
The objector says that the genus 'animal' is said of many differing in number, just like the species. Find the examples given: Zayd and 'Amr (two humans) and this horse and that horse (two horses).
The objector aims to show that the definition of species is not exclusive.
2
Locate the key phrase in the definition
Notice the author's definition of species includes 'without the essence' (dūna al-ḥaqīqa). The objector's argument would only work if the definition said 'agreeing in essence' (muttahidūn bi al-ḥaqīqa).
3
Understand the author's defense
The author explains that 'animal' as a genus answer is valid only when the question involves individuals of different essences (e.g., human and horse). Even if the question includes individuals of the same essence (like two humans), the answer still covers the differing essences present in the overall set.
Thus, the genus does not apply purely because of number difference; it requires essence difference.
4
Analyze the additional denial
The author adds that even the occurrence of the objection is denied, because the answer 'animal' is given because the question includes two different essences (human and horse). The agreeing individuals (e.g., two humans) are treated as one essence for the answer.
This reinforces that the distinction is about essence, not mere number.

(2) For if one says 'What is Zayd and Khalid?' it is valid to say about them 'animal', and likewise 'What is this horse? and this horse?' one says 'animal' - so the definition of species is not exclusive because genus is said of many differing in number as well.

(4) That is: from genus and its likes.
(5) When the answer to 'What is Zayd and Khalid?' and 'This horse and that horse' is our saying 'animal', the answer is due to the existence of difference of essences between individuals of humans and individuals of horses, while it includes those agreeing in essence, namely Zayd and Khalid - they agree in essence - and this horse and that horse likewise.

(2) That is: against his definition of species (as 'a universal said of many differing in number without the essence') is also denied.
(3) That is: when one answers the saying of the questioner 'What is Zayd and 'Amr?' and 'This horse and that horse?' by saying 'animal', the answer is not directed at those differing in essence, but rather because the genus, namely animality, exists within the individuals of humans, and likewise within the individuals of horses - they are two different essences; because the essence of Zayd and 'Amr is other than the essence of horse and this horse; because the individuals of this are other than the individuals of that. So the answer will be about two different essences, and the individuals of the species agree in essence, so there is no objection to his definition.
